<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_and_notoriety">Controversy and notoriety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dungeons_%26_Dragons&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Controversy and notoriety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons_controversies" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons controversies">Dungeons &amp; Dragons controversies</a></div>
<p>At various times in its history, <i>Dungeons &amp; Dragons</i> has received negative publicity, in particular from some <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> groups, for alleged promotion of such practices as <a href="/wiki/Satanism#Theistic_Satanism" title="Satanism">devil worship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a>, suicide, and murder, and for the presence of naked breasts in drawings of female humanoids in the original <i>AD&amp;D</i> manuals (mainly monsters such as <a href="/wiki/Harpy" title="Harpy">harpies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Succubus_(Dungeons_%26_Dragons)" class="mw-redirect" title="Succubus (Dungeons &amp; Dragons)">succubi</a>, etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-Moral_Panic_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moral_Panic-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-attacks_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-attacks-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> These controversies led TSR to remove many potentially controversial references and artwork when releasing the 2nd Edition of <i>AD&amp;D</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dragon_154_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dragon_154-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Many of these references, including the use of the names "<a href="/wiki/Devil_(Dungeons_%26_Dragons)" title="Devil (Dungeons &amp; Dragons)">devils</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Demon_(Dungeons_%26_Dragons)" class="mw-redirect" title="Demon (Dungeons &amp; Dragons)">demons</a>", were reintroduced in the 3rd edition.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Moral_panic" title="Moral panic">moral panic</a> over the game led to problems for fans of <i>D&amp;D</i> who faced social ostracism, unfair treatment, and false association with the occult and <a href="/wiki/Satanism" title="Satanism">Satanism</a>, regardless of an individual fan's actual religious affiliation and beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-Gagne_2018_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gagne_2018-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Dungeons &amp; Dragons</i> has been the subject of rumors regarding players having difficulty separating fantasy from reality, even leading to <a href="/wiki/Psychotic" class="mw-redirect" title="Psychotic">psychotic</a> episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-Darlington_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Darlington-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The most notable of these was the saga of <a href="/wiki/James_Dallas_Egbert_III" title="James Dallas Egbert III">James Dallas Egbert III</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hately_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hately-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> the facts of which were fictionalized in the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Mazes_and_Monsters_(novel)" title="Mazes and Monsters (novel)">Mazes and Monsters</a></i> and later made into a <a href="/wiki/Mazes_and_Monsters" title="Mazes and Monsters">TV movie</a> in 1982 starring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-attacks_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-attacks-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-O&#39;Connor_1982_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O&#39;Connor_1982-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> The game was blamed for some of the actions of <a href="/wiki/Chris_Pritchard" class="mw-redirect" title="Chris Pritchard">Chris Pritchard</a>, who was convicted in 1990 of murdering his stepfather. Research by various psychologists,<sup id="cite_ref-Svitavsky_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Svitavsky-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> starting with Armando Simon, has concluded that no harmful effects are related to the playing of <i>D&amp;D</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Simon_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simon-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The game's commercial success was a factor that led to <a href="/wiki/Lawsuits" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawsuits">lawsuits</a> regarding distribution of <a href="/wiki/Royalties" class="mw-redirect" title="Royalties">royalties</a> between original creators Gygax and Arneson.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Gygax later became embroiled in a political struggle for control of TSR which culminated in a court battle and Gygax's decision to sell his ownership interest in the company in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Dungeons &amp; Dragons</i> has, however, been cited as encouraging people to socialize weekly or biweekly,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> teaching problem solving skills which can be beneficial in adult life, and teaching positive moral decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_products">Related products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dungeons_%26_Dragons&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Related products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons-related_products" class="mw-redirect" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons-related products">Dungeons &amp; Dragons-related products</a></div>
<p><i>D&amp;D'</i>s commercial success has led to many other related products, including <a href="/wiki/Dragon_(magazine)" title="Dragon (magazine)"><i>Dragon</i> Magazine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dungeon_(magazine)" title="Dungeon (magazine)"><i>Dungeon</i> Magazine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons_(TV_series)" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons (TV series)">animated television series</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons_(film)" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons (film)">film series</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons_(album)" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons (album)">official role-playing soundtrack</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons_(novels)" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons (novels)">novels</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> and numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dungeons_%26_Dragons_computer_and_video_games" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Dungeons &amp; Dragons computer and video games">computer and video games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Hobby and toy stores sell dice, miniatures, adventures, and other game aids related to <i>D&amp;D</i> and its game offspring.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dungeons_%26_Dragons&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons_in_popular_culture" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons in popular culture">Dungeons &amp; Dragons in popular culture</a></div>
<p><i>D&amp;D</i> grew in popularity through the late 1970s and 1980s. Numerous games, films, and cultural references based on <i>D&amp;D</i> or <i>D&amp;D</i>-like fantasies, characters or adventures have been ubiquitous since the end of the 1970s. <i>D&amp;D</i> players are (sometimes pejoratively) portrayed as the epitome of <a href="/wiki/Geek" title="Geek">geekdom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> and have become the basis of much geek and gamer humor and satire.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> "In 2017, 9 million people watched others play D&amp;D on Twitch, immersing themselves in the world of the game without ever having to pick up a die or cast a spell".<sup id="cite_ref-:4_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons_in_popular_culture#Players" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons in popular culture">Famous <i>D&amp;D</i> players</a> include Pulitzer Prize winning author <a href="/wiki/Junot_D%C3%ADaz" title="Junot Díaz">Junot Díaz</a>, professional basketball player <a href="/wiki/Tim_Duncan" title="Tim Duncan">Tim Duncan</a>, comedian <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert" title="Stephen Colbert">Stephen Colbert</a>, and actors <a href="/wiki/Vin_Diesel" title="Vin Diesel">Vin Diesel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robin_Williams" title="Robin Williams">Robin Williams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <i>D&amp;D</i> and its fans have been the subject of spoof films, including <i><a href="/wiki/Fear_of_Girls" title="Fear of Girls">Fear of Girls</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-joy001_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joy001-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gamers:_Dorkness_Rising" title="The Gamers: Dorkness Rising">The Gamers: Dorkness Rising</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The original game used <a href="/wiki/Dice_notation" title="Dice notation">3d6</a> in the order rolled (Gygax, Arneson; <i>Dungeons &amp; Dragons</i>). Variants have since been included (Gygax; <i>Dungeon Masters Guide</i>, p. 11) and the standard for more recent editions is "rolling four six-sided dice, ignoring the lowest die, and totaling the other three" (Tweet, Cook, Williams; <i>Player's Handbook</i> [3.0], p. 4), arranging the results in any order desired. Recent editions also allow for a "point buy" system.</span>
</li>
